    <li> Before I talk about the product itself, I feel that it is important to mention the over-exaggerated topic of toluene. Whenever a \\&quot;health scare\\&quot; like this comes up, I always do the research. After reading so many reviews complaining about this horrible ingredient, I thought to myself, \\&quot;If it&#x27;s so bad, then why are the FDA allowing it into products at all?\\&quot; Sure, many brands have removed the ingredient, but if it were truly unsafe to use for the purpose for which it was intended, it wouldn&#x27;t be allowed in any brand. So after having done some research from reliable, credible sources, I stumbled across a few facts.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;First of all, toluene is not cancer causing - so no need to worry about that. Over exposure to the ingredient can cause heart and neurological damage. For this reason alone, a warning label HAS to go on the box. It&#x27;s the same with paint thinners, gasoline, lacquers, and other industrial products made with the ingredient (or any known harmful ingredient) that the warnings be printed on the product. Please be aware that serious side effects are the result of OVER EXPOSURE and that regular, intended usage is nothing at all to be concerned about. The quantity of the ingredient is so low, the only way you&#x27;d really do damage is if you sat there and huffed the bottle. Using it for the purpose of a nail polish top coat is completely safe.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I wouldn&#x27;t necessarily recommend using this if you are pregnant. All of the evidence points to severe effects only occurring with excessive exposure, but this is the only time I personally might not take the risk simply because it is strong-smelling. But overall, use this product as you are supposed to and you&#x27;ll have nothing to worry about. Remember to look at factual sources of evidence, and not automatically assume that someone&#x27;s anecdotal \\&quot;knowledge\\&quot; is somehow more accurate. You don&#x27;t even have to take my word for it; the sources are out there for you to research.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The product itself, as most others have mentioned, is fantastic. Dries within seconds and it&#x27;s such a relief not to feel like I can&#x27;t touch anything for several hours! This is the first bottle I&#x27;ve used, but so far it is my HG of top coats. My nails are hard, dry, and don&#x27;t chip with this stuff on. In fact, it&#x27;s somewhat hard to take the polish off when you&#x27;re ready! I cannot find a single thing wrong with this product and will continue to buy it for as long as it&#x27;s made.ers have mentioned, is fantastic.     <li> I originally tried this product based solely on its description on another website. The idea that it penetrates all layers of polish to make one, solid covering sounded intriguing. Add to that the \\&quot;self-leveling\\&quot; properties and quick-dry claims and I was sold.    Fast forward to when I finally got around to purchasing it. The first time I topped off my carefully executed manicure with this delectable treat, I knew I would never use another top coat ever again. It brushed on so smoothly, leveling everything off beautifully. As I continued to use this product over the course of dozens of manicures and pedicures, I grew to love it more and more. It would even out creases caused by my carelessness and still leave me with a glass-like finish that dried lickety-split.    Now, one thing I MUST point out is that, over time, this product will begin to thicken due to evaporation. It is IMPERATIVE that you DO NOT attempt to thin it out with acetone or nail polish remover. Seche has been able to pin-point the cause of this thickening and they created [[ASIN:B0017ZDH52 Seche Restore Restoration Thinner .5 fl oz (14 ml)]] to reverse the evaporation. Seche Restore is specifically formulated to replace only those ingredients that have evaporated, restoring the once thick mess back to its former glory.    So, be sure to tightly cap it after every use, and be prepared for it to thicken up. It will happen. It happens to ALL nail polishes and top coats. This one is no different. You&#x27;ll probably just notice it sooner with the Seche Vite because you&#x27;ll be using it ALL THE TIME!</li>

    <li> This is the absolute best topcoat ever made. I&#x27;m always thrilled with it! A few important tips. First, you MUST apply this gently, while your base color is still wet. The best way is to get a bead of Seche Vite on the end of your brush, and gently smooth it over your nail. You may end up with a tiny bit of shrinkage of the color around your cuticle and edge of your nails, but I personally have not. I&#x27;ve heard some people do. My ONLY gripe about it, is that about halfway through the bottle, it thickens almost too much to use. Its really nothing that a little polish thinner can&#x27;t fix though. Overall, this always gets me compliments on my nails. It has a shellac finish that lasts until I intentionally remove it with polish remover. The easiest way is to unroll a cotton ball, then tear it in half down the middle. Then tear off 10 pieces from that one cotton ball. Pour some remover into the cap from the bottle, dip one end of each piece into the remover, and place each one on your nails. Let it sit for a minute, and all the polish wipes away in one simple swipe (I always use pure acetone. It may take a minute longer with regular remover)!&lt;br /&gt;Hope this helps my fellow polish addicts!</li>

    <li> I absolutely love Seche Vite.  My polish dried quickly and didn&#x27;t give me enough time to do anything to ruin my manicure the way I normally do. I get compliments on my nails all the time.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve read through some of the comments on here, and here are a few observations I&#x27;ve noticed.  First of all, if your Seche Vite is chipping or gets too thick, buy the Seche Restore.  A few drops will restore your topcoat.  DO NOT use nail polish remover, you need the Restore because it will add back in the chemicals that is used in the topcoat.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;As for Seche Vite not working with three-free polishes, I pretty much exclusively use Zoya nail polish, and I do not have a problem with using Seche Vite as the topcoat.  For those who are encountering problems with shrinkage due to their polish being three-free, it might be a good idea to let the polish dry completely. Here&#x27;s what I found online:&lt;br /&gt;Symptoms of toluene exposure include: irritation of the eyes and nose; weakness, exhaustion, confusion, euphoria, dizziness, headache; dilated pupils, lacrimation (discharge of tears); anxiety, muscle fatigue, insomnia; numbness or tingling of the skin; dermatitis. Toluene exposure may cause liver and kidney damage.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Toluene affects the central nervous system, eyes, skin, respiratory system, liver, kidneys. Breathing high levels of toluene during pregnancy has been shown to result in children with birth defects and to retard mental abilities and growth. There is evidence that exposure to toluene at work is associated with spontaneous abortion.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;High concentrations of toluene, usually from use in a confined space or unventilated area, can cause loss of consciousness, respiratory depression and death. Long term and repeated workplace exposure to toluene affect the central nervous system.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of course, most of these things occur only with acute exposure, so &#x27;they&#x27; say.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, the stuff works, that&#x27;s no lie.     <li> Seche is a cult classic in the nail world, so I was excited to try it.  I generally use higher end polishes like Butter London, OPI, China Glaze, Zoya, and others, but have a busy schedule that makes doing my nails a trial without quickdry topcoat.  As a result, I&#x27;ve tried many on the market.  I&#x27;d place Seche Vite in the upper middle end compared to others I have used.  For me, the cons outweigh its pros, so it is not my go-to topcoat.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Pros:&lt;br /&gt;- Dries very quickly - its definitely faster than other topcoats on the market.  I however do think that this is a double edged sword and is likely a contributor to the drawbacks I experienced.&lt;br /&gt;- Has a high glass shine.  This shine lasts as long as the topcoat does, which is definitely a plus.&lt;br /&gt;- Can be found for a reasonable price if you know where to look - online and small shops tend to be much more realistic than major retailers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;- The shrinkage is awful.  The topcoat&#x27;s underwear seems to matter very little in the outcome here.  Nothing feels worse than topping a flawless application and having it look cracked and sloppy because of the topcoat.&lt;br /&gt;- Cracks often are visible in a couple of days.  While this is unnoticable on dark colours, it can really detract from a light or bright colour.&lt;br /&gt;- I&#x27;ve had only a couple of instances where use of this topcoat has not resulted in significant peeling.  This frequent peeling makes subsequent chips large and very difficult to repair.  By a couple of days in, I&#x27;ve had half of a nail peeling off, usually more than one.  This is much worse on my flatter nails.&lt;br /&gt;- This is an extremely smelly topcoat.&lt;br /&gt;- Personally, I think that when I purchase a product that I should be able to get full use of it without the requirement of purchasing an additional product.  Before reaching even halfway into the bottle, you are likely to encounter a goopy, stringy mess that you can barely get on to the brush.  The fact that one must purchase Seche&#x27;s proprietary thinner to be able to get anywhere close to finishing a bottle is a bit deceptive and frustrating.&lt;br /&gt;- Application can be difficult to master, but is definitely possible.  Throw your ideas about thin coats out the window with this one, and you&#x27;re okay.  Because of how fast it dries, you really have to get it right - do-overs or fix-ups are very difficult.&lt;br /&gt;- I found that Seche has a higher tendency to lift polish than others I have tried, even with proper application.  This was surely unnoticable to anyone but myself, but I did find that it sometimes resulted in streaking as well.&lt;br /&gt;- I have noticed a difference in the general condition of my nails using this product over other quick-dry topcoats, even with all other practices remaining the same.  They seem to get dry and peel more easily when I use this regularly.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, I see why people like it.  If I were to only plan on wearing a manicure for one day, such as for a special occasion, this polish&#x27;s drawbacks would be more of a non-issue.  However, I do want to see longer wear with better presentation.  As much as I can appreciate a topcoat that dries as quickly and glossy as Seche, I would rather wait a bit longer or even use two coats of a formula that works better for me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One thing that is clear is that one&#x27;s nail structure and products used with Seche can play a big role in how well it will work for you - it&#x27;s definitely worth a try!e&#x27;s proprietary thinner to be able to get anywhere close to finishing a bottle is a bit deceptive and frustrating.&lt;br /&gt;- Application can be difficult to master, but is definitely possible.     <li> UPDATE 3/6/2016: I decided to give this another try because I actually lost my bottle of Sally Hansen Top Coat. I figured out there&#x27;s a trick to applying it to wet polish. You have to put a LOT of product on the brush. Enough so that it beads at the tip of the brush, and then you GENTLY pull it down the middle of your nail. You do not want the brush to make contact with your polish. The product should be goopy enough to make a sort of barrier between the brush and your nail so your design doesn&#x27;t smear. Try to finish the nail off in 3 strokes, one down the middle, and one down either side. It will level itself out. Try to keep it off your cuticle and skin because it shrinks as it dries and will peel back from your skin and makes the nail more prone to peeling prematurely. This time around I was able to apply a good coat except for one nail that had an excess amount of Seche Vite pool in one corner and as it dried, it wrinkled up. But the rest of my nails turned out good. I have to go to work in an hour and we&#x27;ll see if it can withstand 6 hours of hard labor. EDIT #2: I&#x27;m pleasantly surprised. Glad I gave this top coat another try. It was a busy day at work. Scrubbing countertops with chemical cleaners, stocking the cooler, counting change in the registers, and not a single chip or dent in my nails. I let them dry for 2 and a half hours before going to work. I haven&#x27;t noticed any shrinkage however I don&#x27;t see an advantage to painting wet polish over dry polish. I would rather let my polish dry to avoid accidentally smearing the design, and you have less shrinkage. I feel comfortable upgrading my rating to 4 stars. The picture attached is after I came home from work.  OLD REVIEW: Probably the worst top coat I&#x27;ve used. The directions say you have to apply it to wet nail polish. The brush pulled the colored polish right off my nail, unbeknownst to me, and tainted the entire bottle when I dipped the brush back in for more. There are now streaks of colored nail polish inside my Seche Vite bottle. So it doesn&#x27;t work on dry nails and it definitely does NOT work on wet nails! What a huge fail and waste of money.
